<div id="review_436026304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436026304" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3212850-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491430066p2/3212850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436026304?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/3212850-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3212850-liz?shelf=contemporary-realistic-fiction">contemporary-realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3212850-liz?shelf=let-me-introduce-my-ya-shelf">let-me-introduce-my-ya-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3212850-liz?shelf=review-advance-copies">review-advance-copies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436026304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1114974153728663945"><a href='http://www.elizziebooks.com/2012/10/31/meant-to-be-by-lauren-morrill-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review + Interview here on my blog!</a><br/><br/>This is a book that took me by utter surprise. I was thinking that I would be reading a cute contemporary novel. I hadn't read the description or even heard what it was about. You see, I met Lauren twice before I even thought about requesting it on NetGalley. If her book is as awesome as she is, it has GOT to be a good read.<br/><br/>Let's talk about the book. I was surprised at how much I was like Julia in high school, minus the grades. She's a stickler for rules and MA</span>
  <span id="freeText1114974153728663945" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.elizziebooks.com/2012/10/31/meant-to-be-by-lauren-morrill-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Review + Interview here on my blog!</a><br /><br />This is a book that took me by utter surprise. I was thinking that I would be reading a cute contemporary novel. I hadn't read the description or even heard what it was about. You see, I met Lauren twice before I even thought about requesting it on NetGalley. If her book is as awesome as she is, it has GOT to be a good read.<br /><br />Let's talk about the book. I was surprised at how much I was like Julia in high school, minus the grades. She's a stickler for rules and MAPS. Oh my gosh, maps are so important. There were times when this got in the way of a true London adventure, and that's when Jason steps in. <br /><br />How much do I love Jason? I love him a lot. Like, he's up there with Augustus Waters. We meet him as this class clown kind of character, and as we move along through the story, we get to know more about him. I need to point out that he doesn't change. He doesn't go from being class clown to the guy who spouts bits of poetry and history when only Julia is listening. He is both. I seriously could shed a tear for how beautiful his character is. Oh, especially with the super awesome amazing twist at the end. It's one of those that will make you shoot out of your chair and yell, "NO WAY!" at 2am. Oh, just me? Oh… Okay.<br /><br />There were some AMAZINGLY WRITTEN LINES. Well, the whole book is so good, but oh, there are some things that Jason says that are so A+. And when Julia has her epiphanies after being wrapped around the axle about the whole "meant to be" issue and the boys issue and the… Okay, she's a worrier. But I have felt some of the same things she's felt, so there were times when I was crying with her. Not TFiOS cries by any means, but I just… When you have felt those same things, it's like finding a new friend to confide in. Seriously, this book. It makes me want more from this author as soon as possible!<br /><br />Overall, this book was pretty freakin' spectacular. Holy wow, as Julia would say! If you're looking for a book that is along the lines of Anna and the French Kiss and Thirteen Little Blue Envelopes, this is your book. Go get it November 13th!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1114974153728663945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2113994302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2113994302" />
    <a title="Dawnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36293066-dawnie"><img alt="Dawnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464172620p2/36293066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2113994302?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawnie" href="/user/show/36293066-dawnie">Dawnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36293066-dawnie?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2113994302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7949651374203233129">2,5 stars<br/><br/>WARNING: RANTING AHEAD!<br/><br/>This book is a bit of a contradiction to me. <br/><br/>Its cute buts also its literary every romance cliche in existence stuffed into a book.<br/>Its a good plot, but SO predictable with everything that happens.<br/>It has nice characters, but at the same time they are so overdone. <br/>The pacing was good, but at the same time there was always something missing. <br/><br/>Its just... a strange book in a way. <br/>Its not bad. Its actually pretty good. <br/><br/>But it could be so much better if the author wouldn</span>
  <span id="freeText7949651374203233129" style="display:none">2,5 stars<br /><br />WARNING: RANTING AHEAD!<br /><br />This book is a bit of a contradiction to me. <br /><br />Its cute buts also its literary every romance cliche in existence stuffed into a book.<br />Its a good plot, but SO predictable with everything that happens.<br />It has nice characters, but at the same time they are so overdone. <br />The pacing was good, but at the same time there was always something missing. <br /><br />Its just... a strange book in a way. <br />Its not bad. Its actually pretty good. <br /><br />But it could be so much better if the author wouldn't have tried so very, very hard to try to be funny at every turn. <br /><br />I mean you can only tumble, stumble or fall into stuff so often before it just gets annoying. yes we get it the main characters is a bit of a klutz. Thanks. <br /><br />And since i am already talking about her, lets continue on with her. <br />I LOVED her at the beginning. <br />I loved that she was so organised. That she loved to read. That she was exited to go on a school trip to LEARN. To experience something she might never get another chance to do. I love that she plans out everything, that she loves guide books and maps and plans and informational templets! I love that she organises everything a specific way. She loves rules and tries to follow them as best as she can because... (well i can guess that it makes her feel better and save and just sure of how things will go because RULES!)<br />I CAN RELATE!<br />And it was BEAUTIFUL to see it in a character. <br /><br />Sadly not even three chapters into the book that side of the character kind of just... got dropped?<br />We got very small little mentioned two or three times through the rest (most) of the book but that specific version of this character we where introduced to at the start? PUFF! She was gone. <br />And i HATED that. <br />Why give me this great character and than just... change her completely?<br />Make her into something so different that it makes no real sense at all?<br /><br />I don't understand the complete and very, very strange and unexplained and unexplainable switch she went through. How can you love plans and schedules and the next second you have no problem with doing everything spontaneous? IT DOES NOT WORK LIKE THAT!<br />Even if someone that really does love plans lets them drop for a little while, lets face it planners will always get back to what they know and love!<br /><br />Okay.... lets end this rant!<br />I didn't like how Morrill made a great and different female main character only to completely change her so specific characteristics after just a handful of pages. <br />Why even start her out like that than????<br /><br /><br />Also how FAN-freaking- TASTIC does Jason has to look (or smell, maybe? Who knows? Maybe he has some kind of bewitching odor that makes every female go crazy!) to be that loved by every female in smelling range of him?<br />He is describe to run around in ripped jeans, old t-shirts and baseball cap. And while i personally don't have anything against that look i also don't necessary look after guys that run around like that ... maybe i am an exception. Possibly. Could be. <br /><br />I didn't get it but okay. <br /><br /><br />I really didn't like the complete idiotic romantic notions in this book and how the romance was build up in this book. <br />I HATED that the main female -lets remember the well planed out and logical and rational person from the first few pages!- is apparently someone that believes completely in finding the perfect one person that everyone has out there. <br /><br /><br />There were just a good amount of completely frustrating moments in this book that made me actual and really angry. Can't explain it really. <br /><br />But the mixture of stupidly behaving hormonally driving teenagers and overused cliches just didn't sit that great with me. <br /><br /><br />Still overall this book isn't bad. <br />Its just not what i wanted it to be. <br /><br />And sadly i saw a lot of potential but it just felt way too forced in so many ways, too overdone and just way to much like trying too hard to be something it just wasn't that it wasn't better than an "okay i read that...." kind of book for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7949651374203233129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1173099742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1173099742" />
    <a title="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages"><img alt="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585465596p2/35614518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1173099742?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" href="/user/show/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages">Chesca (thecrownedpages)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385741781" href="/book/show/17797365-meant-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages?shelf=qbc-2017-2nd-quarter-contemporary">qbc-2017-2nd-quarter-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1173099742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3175040705891423409"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 stars<br/>Read for The Quarterly Book Club’s 2017 2nd Quarter: Contemporary Fiction</b><br/><br/>Lauren Morrill’s <i>
  <b>Meant to Be</b>
</i> is an adventure, across London, following “Book Licker” Julia and her nemesis, Jason, as they search for Chris, a guy she supposedly met one night when Jason dragged her out of their hotel and into a party. For the first time in her life, Julia started breaking rules and maybe, along the way, she would finally find her MTB.<br/><br/>I know that the plot was undeniably cliché wi</span>
  <span id="freeText3175040705891423409" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 stars<br />Read for The Quarterly Book Club’s 2017 2nd Quarter: Contemporary Fiction</b><br /><br />Lauren Morrill’s <i>
  <b>Meant to Be</b>
</i> is an adventure, across London, following “Book Licker” Julia and her nemesis, Jason, as they search for Chris, a guy she supposedly met one night when Jason dragged her out of their hotel and into a party. For the first time in her life, Julia started breaking rules and maybe, along the way, she would finally find her MTB.<br /><br />I know that the plot was undeniably cliché with its theme of enemies-to-lovers romance involving a nerd girl and a popular guy, but this has been recommended to me multiple times that I had to read it.<br /><br />I have mixed and tempestuous feelings towards this book. I have cringed sporadically as I went through this story that I could not believe I was able to finish it and give it this pretty decent rating.<br /><br />The characters were very immature, acting like seven-year olds. Julia was self-centered and thought that almost everyone else was just ridiculous and annoying. She was also too in love with the idea of finding her MTB (Meant-to-be) because of her strong admiration for her parents’ romance. She was craving her own happy ending and her expectations were so unrealistic. Jason was like a kid who swallowed a sack of sugar. I just don’t get it why Julia was the <i>only</i> person who was annoyed by him. He’s the kind of guy you want gagged and tied up but not in a kinky way.<br /><br />What made this book less awful was how informative it was through the trivia about London speckling its pages. I loved that I was also learning as I got to unravel Jason and Julia’s story.<br /><br />Now with regards to the ending, I honestly do not understand how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Julia and Jason ended up with each other. They’ve said very hurtful and mean things to one another and I do not find it swoon-worthy, respectable, or admirable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> What saved this book from receiving a 1-star rating from me was the twist in the end. I did not expect it! That was a good one.<br /><br />So, overall, I guess this book wasn’t that appalling. It got better in the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3175040705891423409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_795691443" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/795691443" />
    <a title="Saoirse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19268890-saoirse"><img alt="Saoirse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476330593p2/19268890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/795691443?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saoirse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saoirse" href="/user/show/19268890-saoirse">Saoirse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=cardboard-characters">cardboard-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=trvl">trvl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=got-me-frustrated">got-me-frustrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=didn-t-work-out-for-me">didn-t-work-out-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=ya-standalone">ya-standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=annoying-heroines">annoying-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=damn-thee-covers">damn-thee-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=gave-up-on">gave-up-on</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19268890-saoirse?shelf=books-i-want-to-hurl">books-i-want-to-hurl</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer795691443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4052323126905057172"><b>DNF @ 50%</b> because it was turning to be awfully boring and tedious.<br/><br/>Well, there goes my patience. It’s been desiderating out of my system as far as I could remember. I mean, don’t get me wrong. <b>This wasn’t a horrible book. </b> The opening cred actually caught my attention (because I love flying and I find it funny for Julia to be scared) but it just didn’t sit well with my other contemporaries. <b>It didn’t exactly scream for me.</b> And I’m finding this odd though because I’m consecutively reading contempo</span>
  <span id="freeText4052323126905057172" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 50%</b> because it was turning to be awfully boring and tedious.<br><br>Well, there goes my patience. It’s been desiderating out of my system as far as I could remember. I mean, don’t get me wrong. <b>This wasn’t a horrible book. </b> The opening cred actually caught my attention (because I love flying and I find it funny for Julia to be scared) but it just didn’t sit well with my other contemporaries. <b>It didn’t exactly scream for me.</b> And I’m finding this odd though because I’m consecutively reading contemporaries that involves travelling somewhere in Europe that concerns with Shakespeare’s plays. (Maybe it’s a sign? ^_^) That waned my interest for <i>Meant To Be</i> because no shit, this book is an absolute replica of the other contemporary books I’ve read with different characters and different stories but the same plot: a shy girl breaking out of her shell and found love in a foreign place. This is so cliché in so many levels. I simply cannot understand the hype these days.<br><br>The painful reality is this book could have been a lot of fun. Sure, there are some points where the MC (Julia) tries to make an inside joke and corny lines. The idea was there but most of the time <b>I find it impossibly hard to find a certain situation funny.</b> I could not relate at all. Nothing was funny. This book tries so hard to be sweet and fluffy–the perfect combo for a cotton candy in a carnival. But blech, it was excruciatingly gray for me. The more I dug in deeper into the story, the more I blink back tears whilst fighting against my heavy eyelids. So for the most part, I was just skimming all throughout. I didn’t exactly DNF this but I consider myself seriously reading the first half and blatantly rolling my eyes while skimming the other half.<br><br>Julia (Le Book Licker) is off to a London adventure with her English Lit class for a ‘field trip’. While the rest of the class is busy thinking about shopping in Lucullan shops, out hobnobbing with a bunch of corps d’elites, and ‘snogging’ (apparently it’s British! *gasps* Oh Julia, you smart, smart girl) sexy Brit dudes, Julia is busy sticking her head on a guidebook to everything London. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hence the name Book Licker. No kidding! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She’s making sure to make this learning experience worthwhile while trying to subdue that GPA. That is, until her English teacher started pairing the class and ended up with her long time nemesis, Jason.<br><br>Here’s how it goes down: Julia hates Jason. He’s irresponsible, idiotic, completely oblivious, flirty, and all the things Julia hates. (Oh and he calls her Book Licker.) At the same time, Jason doesn’t really like Julia that much at all. While he didn’t specifically say he hates Julia, he definitely didn’t say he liked her at all. Why should he when Julia is a no-fun buddy, she makes no friends throughout the trip, she doesn’t socialize, she comes off awkward and clumsy and DOESN’T know the word fun just because she likes to stick with the rules. (WHY OH WHY do they have to make characters who like to read stupid and gets called on for being no-fun? :( It’s becoming insulting, really) It’s a hate-hate relationship between them. They live in different time zones and different poles.<br><br>Now, this is the part I don’t quite fully understand. Jason, who obviously showed no signs of disappointment after being paired with Julia, suddenly asks her to go to a party since they’re supposedly ‘buddies’ and all, and should one get lost, the other one is blamed. Julia does go to the party, partly because Jason has a point but what conflicts me is the way she freaking transform from this simple girl into Aphrodite overnight?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399098628ra/9507109.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book didn’t actually say Julia looked horrible to the extent of not having someone to possibly hook up with but how the hell did she manage to pull that off? Considering being a nerd and all, and that she was described to be ‘plain’ and gets second-hand clothes (not that it’s bad or anything ^_^), that must require a lot of work. I mean, will prep boys be all over me just by wearing four-inched heels and a hitched-up far too skimpy mini skirt?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399098628ra/9507110.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Uh. Will that make me a supermodel too, Tyra?<br><br>And as far as the book goes, it has been nothing but ultimate snores. It was so boring. I want to chuck this out of the window and hit a skunk. If it weren’t for that cover, I would’ve done it a long time ago. We are dragged into Julia and Jason’s adventures to finding Julia’s secret admirer she hooked up with at that stupid party. They had some leads but the author kept diverting them in different directions. It’s frustrating! The thing is, I get why that has to take place. I’m awfully glad this isn’t insta-love because that would certainly be dreadful. I get that the hate-love relationship has to develop at some point by letting Jason and Julia play two-by-two. But the way the author put it is nothing exciting.<br><br>There was no chemistry. There was no ‘my heart is strangely beating for this odd creature in front of me’ thing. There was nothing interesting in their relationship. I don’t even think they had this connection. It was empty, completely devoid of any giggle-worthy moments.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399098628i/9507111.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Did I also mention the believability factor for this book? Why, let’s see: Julia apparently is still crushing on with this kid she wed herself to at age six. (His name is Mark, by the way. It’s kind of hard not to notice that because it’s like in every place.) She believes he’s her MTB (Meant To Be).<br><br><b>Fun Fact:</b> MTB is a girl thing.<br><br>Or so. That’s what Jason says. WTF? Sexist much? Like boys don’t think about the woman of their dreams?<br><br>And anyway, if you think crushing on someone for so long hardly changes a thing, boy, do tell me how to keep it longer. Trust me, it never does. Regardless if the two of you are constantly together at all costs. The fact that this happened to Julia ten years ago and that the guy moved out of town several years ago and have barely had any conversations/communication ever since, whatever feeling Julia has is completely delusional.<br><br>The author doesn’t think so though. Jason suddenly ignores Julia <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[after some shit happened between them (i.e. kissing) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and her secret admirer is still behind the curtain. Guess who shows up at the right time? Mark, of course! It’s like the author ran out of any love-interests that she resorted to bringing the least susceptible (HA. Who am I kidding?) character for our damsel in distress.<br><br>This is where I left off, unfortunately, after suffering from a series of eye rolls this book got from me. There is nothing special here. I most certainly had wanted a cute, swoony romance. The hype is something though because I’m a contradictory person. I think differently, they think differently, you think differently, it doesn’t matter.<br><br>All in all, <b>a stereotypical book that doesn’t focus on an actual plot but on the romance</b> between so-so interesting characters. If you’re up for some ‘Yoohoo! Come on and chase me, luv’ kind of appeal to your plate, go ahead and indulge. If you don’t want to wait like me, keep on dreaming. It ain’t going to happen.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_3565496144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3565496144" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9774002-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606225678p2/9774002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3565496144?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/9774002-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3565496144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5646007535679448979">*Spoilers*<br/><br/>I just wasted so much of my time. And the worst part about that is that while I was reading this book, I was fully aware of that fact and... I didn't stop... *silent scream to the Elder Gods*<br/><br/>I feel like I always have this problem - I pick up these books that have descriptions like: "Hi! My names Bernadette. My name gets me bullied a lot along with my personality but that's only because I'm QUIRKY and TOO SMART COMPARED TO THE REST OF THE BELOW AVERAGE PLEBS IN MY HIGH SCHOOL. But among</span>
  <span id="freeText5646007535679448979" style="display:none">*Spoilers*<br><br>I just wasted so much of my time. And the worst part about that is that while I was reading this book, I was fully aware of that fact and... I didn't stop... *silent scream to the Elder Gods*<br><br>I feel like I always have this problem - I pick up these books that have descriptions like: "Hi! My names Bernadette. My name gets me bullied a lot along with my personality but that's only because I'm QUIRKY and TOO SMART COMPARED TO THE REST OF THE BELOW AVERAGE PLEBS IN MY HIGH SCHOOL. But among all the dumb kids in my school, there's one person I hate above all the others. He's funny, everybody likes him (EXCEPT FOR ME BECAUSE I'M QUIRKY), and he's relentlessly mean to me. But I think I might love him. Mainly because of the aforementioned descriptions of his personality and also because he's HOT. Boo. What am I gonna do?"<br><br>And I don't really think that it's the fault of anyone but my crippling need to buy every single book that I lay eyes. Not only that but I go into these books with an almost childlike naivety, hoping, desperately that one day I'll come across the Golden Grail. That definitely was not this book.<br><a href="https://imgur.com/b3aDneG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601109158ra/30154822.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Remember that description I punched out before? Julie is all of those things with an added side of OCD (she takes obsessive notes on every single tour that they go through in London) and an extra serving of sexism. When I say that she embodies every bad thing in one human being what I mean is that I would rather sit down on the sidewalk and saw off my own legs with the beak of a duck than have to walk anywhere near her. She REPEATEDLY slut shames her female classmates, openly looking down her nose at them when they flirt with boys and idk, just act like teenagers?<br><br>But Julie wants to be edgy. She wants to travel down the bad boy road. (In secret, of course. She would never let her classmates now that her cheeks are anything but CLENCHED around the ten foot pole.)<br><br>So... what does she do? She follows her tour buddy, Jason to a party, gets kind of wasted but not wasted enough to make her look anything but fabulous as she walks home. And then she lies to as many people as she can about being a supermodel.<br><a href="https://imgur.com/KhQzMWG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601109158ra/30154824.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Things obviously spiral out of control pretty quickly from there because... I mean...<br><a href="https://imgur.com/g7cmQtY" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601109158ra/30154821.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>So we're booping along with Julie as she juggles three different guys - the one she lied to, the imaginary one that she kind of creepily obsesses over, and... Jason. Oh Jason.<br><br>When I say that I desperately wanted to like him, what I mean is that for the better part of half of the book, I was clinging onto him like a waterlogged sailer watching her ship go down.<br><br>And then, much like Rose, Jason tenderly pried my fingers away from our raft and let me slowly drift to the bottom of the ocean. It was lovely.<br><br>Jason was one of the most obnoxious, weirdly privileged white boys I have ever had the displeasure of reading. He constantly called her "book licker" which I have to say is probably one of the most disgusting, <i>dumbest</i> nicknames I've heard. And then *deep breath* we have the moment when her imaginary crush suddenly shows up at the hotel their staying in and asks Julie out. Jason has to go because their tour buddies and...<br><a href="https://imgur.com/CroWRra" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601109158ra/30154823.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>He starts to cartwheel around places, doing handstands, jumping on benches all in a bid to... idk. Win Julie's love?<br><br>And then... he bodily throws himself and Julie into a lake. Like... what? Is this teen romance? If this was what I was missing out on in high school than I thank all of the gods because if you've ever been tossed into a lake before... It's fucking awful! But sure. Jason is a huge man-child and he can't fathom any girl (especially one as anal-retentive as Julie) to ever not fall in love with him. Not that he gives her many signals from the constant efforts to get away from her, sneaking out at night to get drunk and mac on girls and generally embarrassing her when they're in large groups.<br><br>Oh. And then there's the little fact that even though he openly complains about not having good grades in his classes and needing them to not get disowned by his family or keep food on his plate, he makes zero effort. Which is one of my pet peeves. Like he just wants to mooch off of everyone for the rest of his life so maybe that's why he likes Julie. She does all of the essays for the trip for both of them. So that's hawt.<br><br>All in all, the two people that I was supposed to like were horrible human beings and the background characters had almost zero likable qualities either. 10 out of 10, would recommend.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9780375990236" href="/book/show/13533686-meant-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=favorites-contemps">favorites-contemps</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297586689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5229585969451535762">OMG, you guys, pardon me while I flail freaking everywhere over how incredibly hilarious and wonderful and perfect for me this book is! Ahhhhh! There are certain authors who are just like made of magic for me, you know? Their every written word speaks to me. They're funny and clever, and say express the things that I think and feel all of the time, and, were I the kind of person to mark up my books, their books would be a mess of notes. Well, Lauren Morrill has just joined that esteemed crew wit</span>
  <span id="freeText5229585969451535762" style="display:none">OMG, you guys, pardon me while I flail freaking everywhere over how incredibly hilarious and wonderful and perfect for me this book is! Ahhhhh! There are certain authors who are just like made of magic for me, you know? Their every written word speaks to me. They're funny and clever, and say express the things that I think and feel all of the time, and, were I the kind of person to mark up my books, their books would be a mess of notes. Well, Lauren Morrill has just joined that esteemed crew with her debut novel Meant to Be.<br /><br />I could tell straight off that this novel would be a fantabulous read for me. The book opens with, "There are certain things in life that just suck. Pouring a big bowl of Lucky Charms before realizing the milk is expired, the word 'moist,' falling face-first into the salad bar in front of the entire lacrosse team . . ." It you can make me laugh with the first two sentences, things are looking up. I proceeded to highlight a bunch of quotes that spoke to me and made me laugh. If you go on GR, right now and look up quotes by Lauren Morrill, I added all of them, because I'm a nutter and obsessed.<br /><br />My very favorite aspect of Meant to Be is how well-drawn Julia is. She totally rocks, but which I mean she's kind of awkward and judgmental and anal-retentive. Julia might have more in common with me than any heroine I've ever encountered, with our main differences being her skill as a swimmer and her dedication to homework. Julia, like me, is not a rule-breaker, pretty much as a rule, and, when she does break them, it's this sort of painful mix of fun and fear. She loves reading more than just about anything else and has only one close friend, Phoebe. On top of that, she's introverted and has curly, frizzy hair she cannot figure out what to do with. My advice to her on that last one is confidence; if you pretend it looks awesome, a lot of people will be fooled.<br /><br />What was most familiar to me about Julia was her perspective. Julia's mental dialog is pretty much exactly what it's like to live in my head, especially my less self-aware high school brain. Despite being incredibly intelligent and witty, Julia, when in a social situation, generally fails to prove herself verbose and lacks witty retorts. Yet, in her head, she has this constant judgmental, snarky commentary running at all times, which, of course, deserts her at times of need. She also has a temper and doesn't realize how harsh or superior she comes off to other people. To me, Julia is one hundred percent realistic, believable and hilarious.<br /><br />I will say that the only other strongly-developed character is Jason, and even he takes a definite back seat. This is no surprise given how caught up Julia is in her own world and impressions of things and people. Since it's just like my mind, I can tell you right now that she's not the most reliable narrator. Meant to Be is definitely driven by Julia, so I suspect that if you don't like her the book won't be much fun for you.<br /><br />The romance does not go anywhere surprising, but it's totally one of my favorite formulas. I've always been so weak to the boy and girl who don't like each other at first plotline, because of my love of Pride and Prejudice, which Morrill is obviously a total fangirl about too, based on the numerous references. Shakespeare comes up a lot too, of course, but, if this is actually a retelling of anything (I thought it was a Shakespeare retelling, though I suspect I made that up), it's of P&amp;P.<br /><br />In Meant to Be, Julia has to deal with a lot of personal issues surrounding her own expectations. She has love built up into this epic construct in her mind, and it's totally messing her up. Again, I relate to this to an insane degree. Her realizations are important ones and I think this sends a great message to teens compared to all of the obnoxious teen love lasts forever stuff. While Jason and Julia do, I think, have amazing chemistry, I also don't know what I see them making a great couple for all time, and I like that.<br /><br />The last thing I must mention is the setting. Meant to Be takes place during a class trip to London. Julia has signed up with out her best friend and is stuck with a whole bunch of other teens she mostly doesn't like while trying to enjoy herself in a foreign country. Girl, I have been there and it is unfortunate, especially since I didn't have a Jason. Meant to Be is one of those books that makes you feel like you're traveling. I already wanted to go to London so, so much, and now I want to just pack up and go right now, though I'm far too plan-oriented for that, as Julia would understand.<br /><br />Though I had a couple of small issues with Meant to Be (mostly to do with the cell phones the school provided for them during the trip, which I so do not see happening), I completely adored the whole book and will be devouring everything else Morrill writes as soon as I possibly can.<br /><br />Read more of my reviews at <a href="http://readeroffictions.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">A Reader of Fictions</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5229585969451535762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1314854670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1314854670" />
    <a title="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5524572-kristin-hackett-superspacechick"><img alt="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481980296p2/5524572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1314854670?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" href="/user/show/5524572-kristin-hackett-superspacechick">Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385741781" href="/book/show/17797365-meant-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1314854670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5443102218168106744">Originally posted on <a href='http://superspacechick.com/2016/01/05/tea-book-chat-meant-to-be-by-lauren-morrill/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Super Space Chick</a>:<br/><br/>Meant to Be by Lauren Morrill is a cute contemporary YA novel that will allow you to feel like you’re on vacation and traveling through London. I’ve been meaning to read this book for ages as it’s been recommended to me by numerous people so I’m glad that I can cross it off my list and now say that I too enjoyed it! The story follows Julia and her high school class who are traveling to London for a week during the year to absorb the culture but sadly her be</span>
  <span id="freeText5443102218168106744" style="display:none">Originally posted on <a href="http://superspacechick.com/2016/01/05/tea-book-chat-meant-to-be-by-lauren-morrill/" rel="nofollow noopener">Super Space Chick</a>:<br /><br />Meant to Be by Lauren Morrill is a cute contemporary YA novel that will allow you to feel like you’re on vacation and traveling through London. I’ve been meaning to read this book for ages as it’s been recommended to me by numerous people so I’m glad that I can cross it off my list and now say that I too enjoyed it! The story follows Julia and her high school class who are traveling to London for a week during the year to absorb the culture but sadly her best friend is unable to attend. She gets stuck being paired with an obnoxious and immature classmate named Jason and from the moment they get on the plane until the very end, hilarity ensues.<br /><br />Meant to Be features a slow burn love / hate romance (my favorite!) but the pacing of the events in the story feel action packed. Throughout the trip, our main character Julia is juggling several men while she sorts out her feelings, something she’s never had to do before and it shows. She can be annoying at times (she’s your typical overachieving know-it-all) but she also has a much softer side that believes in everyone having an MTB (or meant to be). Her partner Jason is one of the most immature YA guys I’ve ever read about and I could easily relate to her frustrations about him. Julia is such a rigid rule follower that a free spirit like Jason often clashes with her in most situations. The one thing I found slightly unbelievable were all of the awkward moments Julia found herself in. It just seemed like too much to happen to one person but despite all of her faults, I found myself rooting for her.<br /><br />My favorite part of this book was exploring London with Julia and Jason. Lauren Morrill makes the reader feel as though they’re also a first time tourist which is something I hadn’t been expecting. They visited a ton of historical sites (such as Stratford-Upon-Avon, The Globe Theater, The London Eye and even Harrod’s) that I’ve always been dying to see but they also spent time during their trip doing several offbeat things which enhanced their cultural experience even further. I found the overall plot to be predictable but it didn’t at all take away from the enjoyment I felt while reading the story. I love witnessing character growth, especially when the main character is an uptight person who’s thrusted out of their comfort zone (and even more especially when said character is experiencing that growth in a place like London). Julia modeled her dream relationship off that of her parents and I loved that comparison throughout the story. Since Julia is away and doesn’t have a ton of access to phone calls she really has to rely on herself to sort out her beliefs and the way she chooses to act which I really appreciated.<br /><br />Final Thoughts: Meant to Be by Lauren Morrill is a darling contemporary novel perfect for anyone looking to lose themselves in a slow burn romance. It’s also ideal for anyone with a case of wanderlust because traveling through London in Morrill’s words is so vivid that it’ll leave you feeling like you’re on a vacation of your own. The plot of the novel is predictable but it’s everything the description and cover promise to be- swoony, engaging and fun!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5443102218168106744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PFWsShQdlkytdzR6accSiEfGi9tirh3g3gkTZAiSDO/0RF5MThk0bVtvk+WF2wpLSSy6ueWIBvB/mnHDLMikVw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sd3HPl4ITr9JbEqbMmFPoLT0evInzc2Yh+P/JdwmDPF5zDU4BAzsnr907QTefVdjuh5LkKDr1ogmcJ2C+HykSQ==')})
  }
